<p><b>Ruud Gullit</b> (<small>Dutch pronunciation:&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[ˈryt ˈxʏlɪt]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nl-Ruud_Gullit.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ad/Nl-Ruud_Gullit.ogg" class="internal" title="Nl-Ruud Gullit.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>;<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> born <b>Rudi Dil</b>; 1 September 1962) is a Dutch <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> manager and former footballer who played professionally in the 1980s and 1990s as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielder</a> or <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">forward</a>. He was the captain of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands national team</a> that was victorious at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1988" title="UEFA Euro 1988">UEFA Euro 1988</a> and was also a member of the squad for the <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 FIFA World Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1992" title="UEFA Euro 1992">Euro 1992</a>.
</p><p>At club level, in 1987 he moved from <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV</a> to <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a> for a <a href="/wiki/World_football_transfer_record" class="mw-redirect" title="World football transfer record">world record transfer fee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Record_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Record-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Easily recognizable with his distinctive dreadlocks and moustache, he was part of the famed Dutch trio at Milan which included <a href="/wiki/Marco_van_Basten" title="Marco van Basten">Marco van Basten</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Rijkaard" title="Frank Rijkaard">Frank Rijkaard</a>. Gullit won three <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> titles and two <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European Cups</a> with Milan. In 1996, he signed for <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> and a year later was appointed the club's player-manager. In his debut season, he led Chelsea to <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> success, the club's first major title for 26 years, and  in so doing became the first overseas manager to win the FA Cup.
</p><p>Gullit won the <a href="/wiki/Ballon_d%27Or" title="Ballon d&#39;Or">Ballon d'Or</a> in 1987 and was named the <a href="/wiki/World_Soccer_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="World Soccer Awards">World Soccer Player of the Year</a> in 1987 and 1989. Normally an <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfielder</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Gullit:_The_Netherlands’_Black_Tulip_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gullit:_The_Netherlands’_Black_Tulip-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> he was a versatile player, playing in numerous positions during his career. In 2004, he was named one of the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_100" title="FIFA 100">Top 125 greatest living footballers</a> as part of <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>'s 100th anniversary celebration.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Gullit was born as Rudi Dil in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> to George Gullit, a <a href="/wiki/Surinamese_people#Emigration" title="Surinamese people">Surinamese</a> migrant who arrived in the Netherlands with <a href="/wiki/Herman_Rijkaard" title="Herman Rijkaard">Herman Rijkaard</a>, father of <a href="/wiki/Frank_Rijkaard" title="Frank Rijkaard">Frank Rijkaard</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and Ria Dil, his <a href="/wiki/Mistress_(lover)" title="Mistress (lover)">mistress</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> from the <a href="/wiki/Jordaan" title="Jordaan">Jordaan</a> district of Amsterdam. The family lived in one split level room on the top floor of a small apartment building. Gullit's father worked as an economics teacher at a local school, his mother as a custodian at the <a href="/wiki/Rijksmuseum" title="Rijksmuseum">Rijksmuseum</a>.
</p><p>Gullit developed his football skills in the confines of the Rozendwarsstraat, and street football was instrumental in his formative years. Gullit's first team were the Meerboys, where he joined as a junior in 1970. At the age of ten, however, Gullit moved from the Jordaan to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Oud-West" title="Amsterdam Oud-West">Amsterdam Old West</a> where he played street football alongside Frank Rijkaard. Gullit joined the <a href="/wiki/AFC_DWS" title="AFC DWS">DWS</a> club after his move, and came to the attention of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_under-17_football_team" title="Netherlands national under-17 football team">Dutch youth team</a>, where he played alongside future full international teammates, <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Koeman" title="Erwin Koeman">Erwin Koeman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Koeman" title="Ronald Koeman">Ronald Koeman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wim_Kieft" title="Wim Kieft">Wim Kieft</a>.
</p><p>It was during his time at DWS that Gullit first took to using his father's surname, rather than his registered surname, as he thought it sounded more like a football player.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He retained his mother's surname, officially, and continues to sign all contracts as Ruud Dil.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="HFC_Haarlem">HFC Haarlem</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: HFC Haarlem">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BanSchoenakerGullit1979.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/BanSchoenakerGullit1979.jpg/220px-BanSchoenakerGullit1979.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/BanSchoenakerGullit1979.jpg/330px-BanSchoenakerGullit1979.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/BanSchoenakerGullit1979.jpg/440px-BanSchoenakerGullit1979.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3664" data-file-height="2436" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BanSchoenakerGullit1979.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gullit (r.) with HFC Haarlem</div></div></div>
<p>In 1978, Gullit signed professionally for <a href="/wiki/HFC_Haarlem" title="HFC Haarlem">HFC Haarlem</a> under coach and former <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a> player <a href="/wiki/Barry_Hughes" title="Barry Hughes">Barry Hughes</a>. Gullit made 91 league appearances for Haarlem, scoring 32 goals. He made his debut for the club at just 16 years old, becoming at the time the youngest player in the history of the <a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In his first year at Haarlem, the club finished bottom of the Eredivisie, but bounced back the <a href="/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_Eerste_Divisie" title="1980–81 Eerste Divisie">following season</a> winning the <a href="/wiki/Eerste_Divisie" title="Eerste Divisie">Eerste Divisie</a>. Gullit was named as the best player in the Eerste Divisie that season.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_Eredivisie" title="1981–82 Eredivisie">1981–82 season</a>, Gullit was in fine form as Haarlem finished fourth and qualified for Europe for the only time in their history. In that same season, Gullit scored the goal he would later consider his finest: "Playing against <a href="/wiki/FC_Utrecht" title="FC Utrecht">Utrecht</a> I went past four defenders and then the goalkeeper, and scored. It was an unforgettable goal for me."<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Hughes was so impressed with the young Gullit that he described him as the "Dutch <a href="/wiki/Duncan_Edwards" title="Duncan Edwards">Duncan Edwards</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Feyenoord">Feyenoord</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Feyenoord">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GullitvanGaal1983.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/GullitvanGaal1983.jpg/220px-GullitvanGaal1983.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/GullitvanGaal1983.jpg/330px-GullitvanGaal1983.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/GullitvanGaal1983.jpg/440px-GullitvanGaal1983.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3674" data-file-height="2447" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GullitvanGaal1983.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gullit (Feyenoord) against <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a> (Sparta) in 1983</div></div></div>
<p>The young Gullit was considered as a signing by English sides <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ipswich_Town_F.C." title="Ipswich Town F.C.">Ipswich Town</a>, but managers <a href="/wiki/Terry_Neill" title="Terry Neill">Terry Neill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Robson" title="Bobby Robson">Bobby Robson</a> turned him down. Neill later told that he considered <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>30,000 too much for "this wild kid".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Gullit therefore moved to <a href="/wiki/Feyenoord" title="Feyenoord">Feyenoord</a> in 1982, where he made 85 league appearances, scoring 31 goals. At Feyenoord, Gullit found himself playing alongside Dutch legend <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff" title="Johan Cruyff">Johan Cruyff</a>, while the assistant manager was <a href="/wiki/Wim_van_Hanegem" class="mw-redirect" title="Wim van Hanegem">Wim van Hanegem</a>, and they were to leave a lasting impression.
</p><p>Gullit's first season saw Feyenoord miss out on major honours, but <a href="/wiki/1983%E2%80%9384_Eredivisie" title="1983–84 Eredivisie">the following year</a> they completed the league and cup double. Gullit was named <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="Dutch Footballer of the Year">Dutch Footballer of the Year</a> in recognition of his contribution to Feyenoord's success. At Feyenoord, Gullit occupied an increasingly advanced role in midfield, having played predominantly as a sweeper at Haarlem.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> While at Feyenoord, Gullit became the focus of a race row as manager <a href="/wiki/Thijs_Libregts" title="Thijs Libregts">Thijs Libregts</a> was alleged to have referred to Gullit as "blackie" and criticised him for being lazy, though Libregts defended himself by claiming that it was merely a nickname.<sup id="cite_ref-Glanville,_p4_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glanville,_p4-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> While playing for Feyenoord at <a href="/wiki/St_Mirren_F.C." title="St Mirren F.C.">St Mirren</a> in September 1983, he was racially abused and spat on by Scottish supporters.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Gullit called it "the saddest night of my life".<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="PSV">PSV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: PSV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruud_Gullit_Face_Shot_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Ruud_Gullit_Face_Shot_2010.jpg/220px-Ruud_Gullit_Face_Shot_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="311" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Ruud_Gullit_Face_Shot_2010.jpg/330px-Ruud_Gullit_Face_Shot_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Ruud_Gullit_Face_Shot_2010.jpg/440px-Ruud_Gullit_Face_Shot_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="1130" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruud_Gullit_Face_Shot_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gullit at a press conference in October 2010</div></div></div>
<p>In 1985, Gullit moved to <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV</a> for 1.2&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Dutch_guilder" title="Dutch guilder">Dutch guilders</a> and wound up scoring 46 goals in 68 league appearances for the team. Gullit was again named Footballer of the Year in 1986 as he helped PSV <a href="/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_Eredivisie" title="1985–86 Eredivisie">capture the Eredivisie</a>  crown, a feat they <a href="/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_Eredivisie" title="1986–87 Eredivisie">repeated the following year</a>. It was at PSV that Gullit really began to establish himself as a world class footballer and his distinctive, dreadlocked appearance made certain that he would catch the eye of Europe's biggest clubs. Gullit was also singled out for criticism by large numbers of Feyenoord supporters, who branded him a "wolf" and accused him of moving to Eindhoven for money.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Milan">Milan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Milan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Silvio_Berlusconi" title="Silvio Berlusconi">Silvio Berlusconi</a> signed Gullit for <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a> in 1987, paying the then <a href="/wiki/World_football_transfer_record" class="mw-redirect" title="World football transfer record">world record transfer fee</a> of 18&#160;million guilders as a replacement for <a href="/wiki/Ray_Wilkins" title="Ray Wilkins">Ray Wilkins</a>. Among his teammates at that club were compatriots <a href="/wiki/Marco_van_Basten" title="Marco van Basten">Marco van Basten</a> and Frank Rijkaard, along with <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Maldini" title="Paolo Maldini">Paolo Maldini</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franco_Baresi" title="Franco Baresi">Franco Baresi</a>. Gullit's exploits with first PSV and then Milan helped him win the <a href="/wiki/Ballon_d%27Or" title="Ballon d&#39;Or">Ballon d'Or</a> award in 1987 which he dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When he arrived at Milan, Gullit initially struggled to settle as he spoke no <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> and was unused to living in a foreign country.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Gullit's first season at Milan, however, saw the club win the <i><a href="/wiki/Scudetto" title="Scudetto">Scudetto</a></i> for the first time in nine years, under coach <a href="/wiki/Arrigo_Sacchi" title="Arrigo Sacchi">Arrigo Sacchi</a>. He was initially used on the right of an attacking trio alongside Van Basten and <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Paolo_Virdis" title="Pietro Paolo Virdis">Pietro Virdis</a>, but after an injury to Van Basten it was changed to a front two. The following season Milan built on their domestic success by adding the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European Cup</a> to their list of honours. Their scintillating 5–0 demolition of <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> in the semi-final second leg came at a cost, as Gullit suffered an injury and required surgery to be fit in time for the final. That performance was followed by a 4–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/FC_Steaua_Bucure%C8%99ti" class="mw-redirect" title="FC Steaua București">Steaua București</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_European_Cup#Final" title="1988–89 European Cup">1989</a> final, with Gullit scoring two crucial goals. The following year, Milan retained the trophy as they defeated <a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica" title="S.L. Benfica">Benfica</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_European_Cup#Final" title="1989–90 European Cup">1990</a> final. However, serious injuries sustained to the <a href="/wiki/Ligament" title="Ligament">ligaments</a> of his right knee limited Gullit's playing time and he managed just two domestic games in the 1989–90 season before appearing in the cup final.
</p><p>In 1990–91, Milan's pursuit of a third consecutive European Cup was cut short by <a href="/wiki/Olympique_de_Marseille" title="Olympique de Marseille">Marseille</a> at the quarter-final stage. Having drawn the first leg at the <a href="/wiki/San_Siro" title="San Siro">San Siro</a>, Milan trailed to a <a href="/wiki/Chris_Waddle" title="Chris Waddle">Chris Waddle</a> goal with little time remaining when the floodlights went out. After a short delay the lighting was restored, but Milan had returned to their dressing room and refused to return to complete the game. <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> awarded Marseille a 3–0 victory and expelled Milan from all European competitions for the following season.
</p><p>While Milan continued their domestic dominance by winning <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> in both <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Serie_A" title="1991–92 Serie A">1991–92</a> (a season in which they went undefeated) and <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_Serie_A" title="1992–93 Serie A">1992–93</a>, Gullit's position was an increasingly peripheral one. This was demonstrated by his omission from the <a href="/wiki/1993_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1993 UEFA Champions League Final">1993 Champions League final</a>, as under the UEFA rules clubs were only allowed to field three foreigners.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sampdoria">Sampdoria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Sampdoria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1993, Gullit moved to <a href="/wiki/U.C._Sampdoria" title="U.C. Sampdoria">Sampdoria</a> and led them to victory in the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Coppa_Italia" title="1993–94 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Serie_A" title="1993–94 Serie A">1993–94 season</a>. He also scored the winner in a 3–2 victory over Milan.
</p><p>Gullit was briefly re-signed by a very impressed Milan in 1994, but quickly returned to Sampdoria before the culmination of the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Serie_A" title="1994–95 Serie A">1994–95 season</a>. During his time, he served under manager <a href="/wiki/Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson" title="Sven-Göran Eriksson">Sven-Göran Eriksson</a> and the two had a strong understanding and mutual respect. In his brief time at Sampdoria, he scored 15 goals.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chelsea">Chelsea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Chelsea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gullit%27s_jersey.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Gullit%27s_jersey.jpg/220px-Gullit%27s_jersey.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Gullit%27s_jersey.jpg/330px-Gullit%27s_jersey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Gullit%27s_jersey.jpg/440px-Gullit%27s_jersey.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gullit%27s_jersey.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gullit's No.4 Chelsea shirt, on display at the <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Bridge_(stadium)#Centenary_Museum" title="Stamford Bridge (stadium)">club museum</a></div></div></div>
<p>In July 1995, Gullit signed for <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> on a free transfer. Initially played as sweeper by manager <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Hoddle" title="Glenn Hoddle">Glenn Hoddle</a> with limited success, Gullit was moved to his more familiar role in midfield, where he scored six goals. The signing of Gullit, alongside the likes of <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hughes" title="Mark Hughes">Mark Hughes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dan_Petrescu" title="Dan Petrescu">Dan Petrescu</a>, propelled Chelsea to the semi-final of the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> but their league form was disappointing.
</p><p>Gullit had some difficulties adapting to the style of play at Chelsea: "I would take a difficult ball, control it, make space and play a good ball in front of the right back, except that he didn't want that pass. Eventually Glenn said to me, 'Ruud, it would be better if you do these things in midfield.'"<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> His adjustment, however, was rapid and he ended the season by being named runner-up to <a href="/wiki/Eric_Cantona" title="Eric Cantona">Eric Cantona</a> as Footballer of the Year.
</p><p>Gullit has since often stated in interviews that it was in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> he enjoyed his career the most and felt happiest: "Every time I played for Chelsea, I thought, 'Nice game, beautiful stadium, great crowd, I'm playing well.' It was the only time I really had fun."<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In moving to Chelsea, Gullit played an important part in the "foreign revolution" as numerous high-profile international stars, such as the Italian superstar <a href="/wiki/Gianfranco_Zola" title="Gianfranco Zola">Gianfranco Zola</a> who became a Chelsea legend, and the Dutch magician <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Bergkamp" title="Dennis Bergkamp">Dennis Bergkamp</a>, joined <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">FA Premier League</a> clubs and helped to increase its worldwide profile.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruud_Gullit_1988.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Ruud_Gullit_1988.jpg/220px-Ruud_Gullit_1988.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="332" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Ruud_Gullit_1988.jpg/330px-Ruud_Gullit_1988.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Ruud_Gullit_1988.jpg/440px-Ruud_Gullit_1988.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2481" data-file-height="3739" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruud_Gullit_1988.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ruud Gullit in 1988</div></div></div>
<p>In 1981, on his 19th birthday, Gullit made his international debut as a substitute for the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands national team</a> against <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a>, a game the Dutch lost 2–1.
</p><p>Gullit's early international career was marred by disappointment as the team failed to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982 FIFA World Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1984" title="UEFA Euro 1984">UEFA Euro 1984</a> - the Netherlands missed out on the latter tournament on <a href="/wiki/Goal_difference" title="Goal difference">goals scored</a> as <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a>, needing an 11-goal victory to qualify, trounced <a href="/wiki/Underdog_(competition)" class="mw-redirect" title="Underdog (competition)">minnows</a> <a href="/wiki/Malta_national_football_team" title="Malta national football team">Malta</a> 12–1 in their final qualifying game.
</p><p>There was further frustration in 1985 when the Dutch missed out on qualification for the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> at the hands of neighbours <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a> in a <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)#Play-offs" title="1986 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">play-off</a>. Having lost 1–0 in Belgium, the Netherlands appeared to be set for qualification in <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> as they led 2–0 until a late <a href="/wiki/Georges_Gr%C3%BCn" title="Georges Grün">Georges Grün</a>  goal put Belgium through on <a href="/wiki/Away_goals_rule" title="Away goals rule">away goals</a>.
</p><p>Gullit, however, was one of the key players for the Netherlands as he helped his country win <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1988" title="UEFA Euro 1988">Euro 1988</a> under coach <a href="/wiki/Rinus_Michels" title="Rinus Michels">Rinus Michels</a>. Having lost their opening game of the tournament to the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_national_football_team" title="Soviet Union national football team">Soviet Union</a>, the Netherlands beat <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a> to reach the semi-finals. After defeating <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">West Germany</a> 2–1 in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, the Netherlands faced the Soviet Union again in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1988_Final" title="UEFA Euro 1988 Final">final</a>. Gullit opened the scoring with a well-placed header and Marco van Basten scored an incredible volley to cap a 2–0 win. Gullit was thus the first Dutch captain to hold aloft international silverware.
</p><p>The Dutch travelled to the <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 World Cup</a> as one of the favourites, but the team failed to perform as expected. Gullit's knee injuries clearly hampered his play, and his only moment of brilliance was a superb dribble and shot against Ireland which helped the Netherlands qualify for the second round. There they met West Germany in one of the most exciting games of the tournament, though the game was marred by an altercation between Frank Rijkaard and <a href="/wiki/Rudi_V%C3%B6ller" title="Rudi Völler">Rudi Völler</a>. The Germans gained revenge for their defeat at Euro 1988 by beating the Netherlands 2–1 and going on to win the tournament.
</p><p>1992 saw the Netherlands again among the favourites for silverware in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1992" title="UEFA Euro 1992">Euro 1992</a>. Gullit appeared in imperious form against <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> in their opening game of the tournament as he supplied <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Bergkamp" title="Dennis Bergkamp">Dennis Bergkamp</a> with an easy goal. But after drawing with <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_football_team" title="Russia national football team">Russia</a> and beating Germany, the Netherlands suffered a shock exit on penalties to <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a>, who ended up winning the championship's <a href="/wiki/Henri_Delaunay" title="Henri Delaunay">Henri Delaunay</a> Trophy.
</p><p>In 1993, Gullit and Netherlands manager <a href="/wiki/Dick_Advocaat" title="Dick Advocaat">Dick Advocaat</a> began what was to be a long-running dispute which ultimately ended Gullit's international career. Advocaat's decision to play Gullit on the right side of midfield in a game against England at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley</a>, rather than his usual central position, upset Gullit and this was exacerbated by his substitution for <a href="/wiki/Marc_Overmars" title="Marc Overmars">Marc Overmars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Glanville,_p4_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glanville,_p4-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Gullit refused to play for the national team following this but later changed his mind and agreed to return, facing Scotland in May 1994. Shortly before the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 World Cup</a>, Gullit walked out of the pre-tournament training camp and would never play international football again. In December 2013, while appearing on Dutch television program <i>Studio Voetbal</i>, Gullit and Advocaat stated they were both at fault in the matter and regretted it.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A complete and versatile player, Gullit epitomised the ethos of <a href="/wiki/Total_Football" title="Total Football">Total Football</a> as he was naturally adept in several positions, and was capable of aiding his team defensively as well as offensively due to his work-rate, ball-winning abilities, and tactical intelligence in addition to his skill and physical qualities.<sup id="cite_ref-AC_Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Ruud_Gullit_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AC_Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Ruud_Gullit-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Normally deployed as an <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfielder</a> or as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Second_striker" title="Forward (association football)">second striker</a>, he was capable of playing anywhere in <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfield</a> or along the <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">front-line</a>, on either <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Winger" title="Midfielder">wing</a> or even in the <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Central_midfielder" title="Midfielder">centre</a>, and could also play as a <a href="/wiki/Sweeper_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweeper (association football)">sweeper</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gullit:_The_Netherlands’_Black_Tulip_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gullit:_The_Netherlands’_Black_Tulip-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Regarded as one of the greatest players of all time,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> his foremost attribute was his athleticism, as he used his strength and speed, combined with his technique, to great effect; he was also strong in the air, as he was tall, powerful, and an excellent jumper.<sup id="cite_ref-AC_Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Ruud_Gullit_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AC_Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Ruud_Gullit-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Yet, unusually for a man of his stature, Gullit was an elegant player, who also possessed outstanding natural balance, poise, technical ability, and <a href="/wiki/Dribbling#Association_football" title="Dribbling">dribbling</a> skills, which gave a graceful style to his game.<sup id="cite_ref-AC_Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Ruud_Gullit_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AC_Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Ruud_Gullit-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Gullit also was noted for his intelligence, creativity, vision, and spatial abilities, qualities that helped him score goals early in his career and enabled him to play in a deeper role as a <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">playmaker</a> late in his days, where he was known for creating chances for teammates.<sup id="cite_ref-AC_Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Ruud_Gullit_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AC_Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Ruud_Gullit-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Gullit thus combined physical presence with flair, mental acuity, formidable technique and natural touch, to become an iconic figure in world football.<sup id="cite_ref-AC_Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Ruud_Gullit_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AC_Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Ruud_Gullit-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Beyond his qualities as a footballer, Gullit also stood for his leadership and tenacity.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Despite his talent, however, he struggled with injuries throughout his career, which later affected his fitness.<sup id="cite_ref-AC_Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Ruud_Gullit_24-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AC_Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Ruud_Gullit-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gullit's brilliance prompted <a href="/wiki/George_Best" title="George Best">George Best</a> to comment in 1990, "Ruud Gullit is a great player by any standards. He has all the skills. He's not afraid to do things with the ball. And he looks as if he's enjoying every second of it. By my reckoning that's what makes him an even better player than <a href="/wiki/Diego_Maradona" title="Diego Maradona">Maradona</a>. Both have the key quality you will find in all the best players: balance. You just can't knock them off the ball. It was the same with <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pelé">Pelé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Beckenbauer" title="Franz Beckenbauer">Beckenbauer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff" title="Johan Cruyff">Cruyff</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Managerial_career">Managerial career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Managerial career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chelsea_2">Chelsea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Chelsea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the summer of 1996, when Glenn Hoddle left Chelsea to become manager of the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national team</a>, Gullit was appointed as a <a href="/wiki/Player-manager" class="mw-redirect" title="Player-manager">player-manager</a>, becoming the first Dutchman to manage in the Premier League.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Gullit made a promising start to his managerial career when in the first season as a player-manager he guided Chelsea to an FA Cup triumph in <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_FA_Cup" title="1996–97 FA Cup">1997</a>, the club's first major <a href="/wiki/1997_FA_Cup_Final" title="1997 FA Cup Final">trophy</a> in 26 years. The club also finished at a creditable <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_FA_Premier_League" title="1996–97 FA Premier League">sixth place</a> in the Premiership.
</p><p>The following season, with Chelsea in second place in the Premiership and proceeding to the quarter-finals in two cup competitions, he was sacked, allegedly for a disagreement with the club's board over compensation, though Gullit himself disputed this.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Gianluca_Vialli" title="Gianluca Vialli">Gianluca Vialli</a>, a man he had helped to bring to the club, and who went on to guide them to <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners&#39; Cup">UEFA Cup Winners' Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">Football League Cup</a> glory over the remainder of the season. Gullit's last appearance as a player came in the first leg of that season's <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">League Cup</a> semi-final against Arsenal, but Gullit was sacked before the second leg.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> After Gullit's controversial sacking by Chelsea, chairman <a href="/wiki/Ken_Bates" title="Ken Bates">Ken Bates</a> famously said of Gullit, "I didn't like his arrogance – in fact I never liked him."<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newcastle_United">Newcastle United</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Newcastle United">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In August 1998, Gullit was named manager of <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> two games into the new league season and reached the <a href="/wiki/1999_FA_Cup_Final" title="1999 FA Cup Final">1999 FA Cup Final</a> in his first year. Fans remained supportive despite a poor run of results, although a well-publicised contretemps with the team's top scorer <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a> and captain <a href="/wiki/Rob_Lee" title="Rob Lee">Robert Lee</a> did not put him in a favourable light.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Gullit even refused to assign Lee a squad number, giving Lee's number 7 to new signing <a href="/wiki/Kieron_Dyer" title="Kieron Dyer">Kieron Dyer</a>. In a match between Newcastle and local rivals <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunderland A.F.C">Sunderland</a> following the latter's return to the Premiership, Gullit left the usual starting strikers Shearer and <a href="/wiki/Duncan_Ferguson" title="Duncan Ferguson">Duncan Ferguson</a> on the bench. Newcastle lost 2–1, and Gullit resigned three days later, five games into the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_FA_Premier_League" title="1999–2000 FA Premier League">1999–2000 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Feyenoord_2">Feyenoord</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Feyenoord">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Before the start of the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Eredivisie" title="2004–05 Eredivisie">2004–05 season</a>, Gullit took charge of Feyenoord, quitting at the end of that season without winning any trophies, being replaced by <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Koeman" title="Erwin Koeman">Erwin Koeman</a>. Feyenoord had finished a disappointing fourth in the <a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a>, behind <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a>, PSV and <a href="/wiki/AZ_Alkmaar" title="AZ Alkmaar">AZ</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Los_Angeles_Galaxy">Los Angeles Galaxy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Los Angeles Galaxy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cobi_Jones_and_Ruud_Gullit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Cobi_Jones_and_Ruud_Gullit.jpg/220px-Cobi_Jones_and_Ruud_Gullit.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Cobi_Jones_and_Ruud_Gullit.jpg/330px-Cobi_Jones_and_Ruud_Gullit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Cobi_Jones_and_Ruud_Gullit.jpg/440px-Cobi_Jones_and_Ruud_Gullit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1344" data-file-height="1433" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cobi_Jones_and_Ruud_Gullit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gullit with <a href="/wiki/Cobi_Jones" title="Cobi Jones">Cobi Jones</a> at Galaxy.</div></div></div>
<p>On 8 November 2007, Gullit became head coach for the <a href="/wiki/LA_Galaxy" title="LA Galaxy">LA Galaxy</a>, signing a three-year contract.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> His <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>2&#160;million per year salary was the highest ever given to a <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a> (MLS) head coach. Gullit arrived as replacement for <a href="/wiki/Frank_Yallop" title="Frank Yallop">Frank Yallop</a> who was let go after Galaxy failed to make the 2007 MLS playoffs despite having record signing <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> on the roster.
</p><p>From the start, Gullit's time with Galaxy was troublesome. Not well-versed in the intricacies and specifics of the MLS such as salary cap and draft rules, the Dutchman never adapted well to the North American league.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The ill-fated acquisition in January 2008 of left back <a href="/wiki/Celestine_Babayaro" title="Celestine Babayaro">Celestine Babayaro</a>, who was signed on Gullit's personal wishes before being dismissed without playing a competitive match, set the tone for the league campaign. Afterlosing 0–4 in the season opener, Gullit clashed with midfielder <a href="/wiki/Peter_Vagenas" title="Peter Vagenas">Peter Vagenas</a>, who criticized him for completely neglecting set play practice during training.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>As the season progressed, Gullit clashed with several players, notably <a href="/wiki/Landon_Donovan" title="Landon Donovan">Landon Donovan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abel_Xavier" title="Abel Xavier">Abel Xavier</a>, the latter who criticized Gullit's managerial style and claimed he did not have respect for most of the players.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> It was later reported that Gullit's appointment had been made in controversial fashion as Galaxy general manager, <a href="/wiki/Alexi_Lalas" title="Alexi Lalas">Alexi Lalas</a>, had been bypassed in the process, with the decision being led by David Beckham's advisers: his management company <a href="/wiki/19_Entertainment" title="19 Entertainment">19 Entertainment</a> and his personal manager <a href="/wiki/Terry_Byrne" title="Terry Byrne">Terry Byrne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 August 2008, Gullit resigned as coach of the Galaxy, citing personal reasons. This came following a seven-game winless streak. General manager Lalas was fired at the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terek_Grozny">Terek Grozny</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Terek Grozny">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 18 January 2011, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Premier_League" title="Russian Premier League">Russian Premier League</a> side <a href="/wiki/FC_Terek_Grozny" class="mw-redirect" title="FC Terek Grozny">Terek Grozny</a> announced that Gullit has agreed to sign a year-and-a-half contract and become the head coach for the Chechen side. Upon signing, Gullit told <i><a href="/wiki/Sovetsky_Sport" title="Sovetsky Sport">Sovetsky Sport</a></i>, "I'd like to believe that I can bring joy into the lives of the Chechen people through football...Of course, I won't deny that I'm getting lots of money from Terek."<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Gullit was sacked by the club on 14 June 2011, having only won three games as manager. The club also said Gullit had a "party lifestyle".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Managerial_statistics">Managerial statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Managerial statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_career">Media career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Media career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arsenal_2_Chelsea_1_(34968568976).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Arsenal_2_Chelsea_1_%2834968568976%29.jpg/220px-Arsenal_2_Chelsea_1_%2834968568976%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Arsenal_2_Chelsea_1_%2834968568976%29.jpg/330px-Arsenal_2_Chelsea_1_%2834968568976%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Arsenal_2_Chelsea_1_%2834968568976%29.jpg/440px-Arsenal_2_Chelsea_1_%2834968568976%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2175" data-file-height="3263" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arsenal_2_Chelsea_1_(34968568976).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gullit in his role as a BBC pundit during the <a href="/wiki/2017_FA_Cup_Final" title="2017 FA Cup Final">2017 FA Cup Final</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1988, Gullit scored a No. 3 hit with the <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">anti-apartheid</a> song "South Africa" in the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Top_40" title="Dutch Top 40">Dutch Top 40</a> together with the reggae band <a href="/wiki/Revelation_Time" title="Revelation Time">Revelation Time</a>. Previously, he had a modest hit in 1984 with the song "Not the Dancing Kind".
</p><p>After his spell at Newcastle, Gullit spent several years working as a football commentator, having previously coined the term "sexy football"<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> during his spell as a <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> pundit for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">Euro 1996</a> while still playing professionally for Chelsea. Gullit used the term to describe teams, such as <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> at that tournament,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> who played attractive football with an emphasis on the defense-penetrating pass-and-move game.
</p><p>By 2006, Gullit had a talk show on Dutch TV, where he has interviewed, amongst others, <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> When Gullit was named winner of the Ballon d'Or in 1987, he dedicated the award to the then imprisoned Nelson Mandela. Gullit has since said in interviews that he met Mandela after he was released, and that Mandela had said to him, "Ruud, I have lots of friends now. When I was on the inside, you were one of the few."<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, Gullit recalled, "Four months ago I visited Robben Island and met three guys who were cell-mates of Nelson Mandela. They remembered me dedicating my award in 1987 to Mandela and they said they couldn’t believe what I had done, and were sure the football authorities would withdraw the award. That's what apartheid did to them, it made them believe injustice was a normal part of life."<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gullit also appeared as a <a href="/wiki/Pundit" title="Pundit">pundit</a> for <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a> and works as an analyst for Champions League games on <a href="/wiki/Sky_Sports" title="Sky Sports">Sky Sports</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera_Sports" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Jazeera Sports">Al Jazeera Sports</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a>, Gullit worked as a studio analyst alongside former players <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Klinsmann" title="Jürgen Klinsmann">Jürgen Klinsmann</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_McManaman" title="Steve McManaman">Steve McManaman</a> for <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> He subsequently worked as an analyst for Al Jazeera Sports during <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a> alongside Glenn Hoddle and Terry Venables, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, Gullit and many other former footballers were brought into <a href="/wiki/EA_Sports" title="EA Sports">EA Sports</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/FIFA_14" title="FIFA 14">FIFA 14</a></i> as "Legends" cards in FIFA Ultimate Team; his card is one of the highest rated in the game.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, Gullit joined BBC's <a href="/wiki/Match_of_the_Day" title="Match of the Day">Match of the Day</a> as a studio pundit and first appeared during the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Premier_League" title="2014–15 Premier League">2014–15 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gullit embarked on the Heineken <a href="/wiki/Uefa_champions_league" class="mw-redirect" title="Uefa champions league">Champions League</a> Trophy Tour in 2016 where he visited Vietnam with <a href="/wiki/Carles_Puyol" title="Carles Puyol">Carles Puyol</a>. During the stop in Vietnam he met lifelong fan Max Caubo; who lived there at the time<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Gullit has been married three times and has six children, two from each of his marriages.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> He is a self-declared Feyenoord supporter.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruud_Gullit&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
